ARIE 1912-1913 [vol. 035]


A.--List of copper-plates examined during 1912-13.


ARIE/1912-1913/A/1912-13/1 (page 13)
Placement
A.H.A.Todd, Esq., I.C.S., Special Settlement Officer, Party No. III, Madanapalle.
Dynasty
Vijayanagara
King
Tirumala-Mahārāya (i.e. Tirumala I).
Date
Śaka 1493, Pra-jāpati, Māgha, su. di. 12.
Language
Sanskṛit (Nāgarī)
Origin
Returned to Mr. Todd.
Edition
To be published in the Ep. Ind.
Remarks
Records the grant of Penuṅgulūru surnamed Yellamarājēndrasamudra, to Brāhmaṇas at the request of Tirumalarāja, one of the chiefs of the Maṭla family which claimed Chōḷa origin.
ARIE/1912-1913/A/1912-13/2 (page 13)
Placement
E.B.Elwin, Esq., I.C.S., Collector of Godavari.

…
King
Śiṅgaya-Nāyaka
Date
Śaka 1290, Śrāvaṇa, solar eclipse.
Language
Sanskṛit (Telugu)
Origin
To be returned to the Collector.
Edition
To be published in the Ep. Ind.
Remarks
Registers the grant of the village Akkala-pūṇḍi surnamed Mummaḍī-Siṅgavaram to a certain Parahitāchārya.

Gift of the village Uṟuvuṭūru evidently situated in Gudrahāra-vishaya, to fourteen Brāhmaṇas.

ARIE/1912-1913/A/1912-13/6 (page 13)
Placement
The Monegar of Daṇḍapalle village.
Dynasty
Vijayanagara
King
Vijayabhūpati
Date
Śaka 1332, Vikṛiti, Bhādrapada, su. di. 11, Monday, Śra-vana, Lakshmī-Nārāyaṇa yōga.
Language
Sanskṛit & Kanarese (Nāgarī)
Origin
To be returned to the Mone-gar.
Edition
Do. By Mr. G.Ven-koba Rao.
Remarks
Registers that the king founded a village called Kṛiyāśaktipura near Daṇḍēhaḷḷi in Huli-nāḍu of the Muḷvāgila-rājya and presented it to a certain Kṛishṇa-Paṇḍi-ta. The latter in his turn, made a gift of the village to Brāhmaṇas.
ARIE/1912-1913/A/1912-13/7 (page 13)
Placement
The Tahsildar of Rāyadrug
Dynasty
Do.
King
Vīrapratāpa-Kṛishṇarāya
Date
Śaka 1446, Tāraṇa, Vaiśākha, su. di. 15.
Language
Sanskṛit & Kanarese (Nāgarī)
Origin
To be returned to the Tahsil-dar.
Edition
…
Remarks
Gift of the village of Pēyalabaṇḍa alias Kṛi-shṇarāyapura, in [Ku]ṟuba-Śīvarasīma which was a district of Niḍugalladurga-rājya, to a certain Nṛisiṁhādhvarin.
ARIE/1912-1913/A/1912-13/8 (page 13)
Placement
The Tahsildar of Harpana-haḷḷi.
Dynasty
Sanskrit (Naga-ri).
King
Tribhuvanamalla Vikramā-ditya VI.
Date
Chāḷukya-Vikra-ma year 12, Prabhava (= A.D. 1087-88) and Chāḷukya-Vikrama year 48, Śōbhakṛit (= A.D. 1123-24).
Language
Sanskṛit (Nāgarī)
Origin
Tobe returned to the Tahsil-dar.
Edition
To be published in the Ep. Ind., by Dr. Fleet, London.
Remarks
Registers grants of the villages of Nirugunda (in Vikkiga seventy, a district of Kōkali 500), Sapava and Kṛishṇapallikā, to certain Brāhmaṇas of the Draviḍa-dēśa, and of the village Ādityapallikā to the god Bhīmēśvaradēva at Sapava.
ARIE/1912-1913/A/1912-13/9 (page 14)
Placement
C.F.Brackenbury, Esq., I.C.S., Special Settlement Officer, Party No. III, Madanapalle.
Dynasty
Vijayanagara
King
Vīrapratāpa Kṛishṇadēvarāya
Date
Śaka 1498, Dhā-tṛi, Māgha, ba. di. 10.
Language
Telugu
Origin
To be returned to the Special Settlement Officer.
Edition
…
Remarks
Kṛishṇarāya's rule never extended so far. Registers that Yādava Narasiṁharāju, Rāmaliṅganāchāri, Kūnapuli, Peddēvi Nāyuḍu and Chinadēvi Nāyuḍu, Raipa Sōmayājulu and Nala-Veṅkaṭareḍḍi of Kasanūru paid their homage to the king with. 50 varāhas and received certain offices and service-inams in the village of Lōmaḍa. The inscription specifies the mirāś, mēra and other income due to the servants of that village.
ARIE/1912-1913/A/1912-13/10 (page 14)
Placement
Do.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Yara-Timmarāja, brother-in-law of Mahādēvarāya, ruling at Vijayanagara.
Date
Śaka 5[6] 9[0], Śārvari (wrong), Vaiśākha, su. di. 15.
Language
Telugu
Origin
To be returned to the Special Settlement Officer.
Edition
…
Remarks
The king is, perhaps, to be identifled with Tirumala I., brother of the famous Rāma-rāja (Hemraj). Registers that two Reḍḍis came from the sea-side (country), with their cattle and children to the village Rāvula-kollu and got permission to construct a village near the hill, by Yara-Timmarāja who was then governing Ghaṇḍikōṭa. Its boundaries were defined and service-ināms settled. The grant was written by Teliki Bālā-Batuḍu.
ARIE/1912-1913/A/1912-13/11 (page 14)
Placement
Do.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Śaka 1508, Vyaya, Vaiśākha, su. di. 15, Monday, lunar eclipse.
Language
Telugu
Origin
To be returned to the Special Settlement Officer.
Edition
…
Remarks
Records that Anugoṇḍa Veṅgaḷappa settled a dispute which arose about the distri-bution of service-inam lands in the village Avuḍūru, between the agrahārikas and the karanams.
ARIE/1912-1913/A/1912-13/12 (page 14)
Placement
Do.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Śaka 1633, Virōdhi, Vaiśākha, su. di. 10.
Language
Telugu
Origin
To be returned to the Special Settlement Officer.
Edition
…
Remarks
The car festivals at Conjeeveram of the gods E1kāmrēśvara and Varadarāja were attended by several chiefs including an officer of Harsadu Aṇarvadikānu-Sāyappu (i.e., Hazrat Anvārudīn Khān Sāheb ?). They found on that occasion that some-thing was wrong with the divine glory of the images. The cause of this not being known they consulted one Kanumanūru Raṅgāchārla. The latter by his magical powers put things right and got from the chiefs the privilege of collecting certain specified annuities from different classes of people living in the 56 countries.
ARIE/1912-1913/A/1912-13/13 (page 15)
Placement
C.F.Brackenbury, Esq., I.C.S., Special Settlement Officer, Party No. III, Madanapalle.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Śaka 1464, Krōdhana (wrong) Bhādrapada, su. di. 10, Thursday and Śaka 1432, Pramōdūta (Pramōda), Māgha, ba. di. 14.
Language
Telugu
Origin
To be returned to the Special Settlement Officer.
Edition
…
Remarks
This is a document which professes to settle certain disputes between Baḍugulavāru and Paināṭi-vīrulu, in the matter of para-phernalia used during public processions. The judges, evidently, were the Śaivas, Vaishṇavas and other great men of Conjeeveram.
ARIE/1912-1913/A/1912-13/14 (page 15)
Placement
Do.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Śaka 1283, Jaya (wrong), Mārgaśira, ba. di. 10.
Language
Telugu
Origin
To be returned to the Special Settlement Officer.
Edition
…
Remarks
The boundaries of the village Kasunūru which was a surname of Tiruveṅgaḷanellūr in Gutti-rājya, are first described. Then follow details of mēra, mirāś and other service-inams granted to village servants. This record pretends to belong to the reign of Prauḍhadēva-Mahārāya (Śaka 1371 to 1387).
ARIE/1912-1913/A/1912-13/15 (page 15)
Placement
The Tahsildar of Hindupur
Dynasty
Vijayanagara
King
Raṅga VI.
Date
Lost
Language
Sanskṛit (Nāgarī)
Origin
To be returned to the Tahsil-dar.
Edition
…
Remarks
Incomplete. The genealogy of the Karṇāṭa kings with which the inscription begins, is identical with that given in the Kaḷḷakurśi grant of Raṅga VI, as far as Veṅkaṭa II. The seal bears the legend śrī-Veṅkaṭēśa.
ARIE/1912-1913/A/1912-13/16 (page 15)
Placement
Do.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Śaka 1109, Jaya (wrong), Āśvija, su. di. 10.
Language
Telugu
Origin
To be returned to the Tahsil-dar.
Edition
…
Remarks
A plain forgery which pretends to be dated in the reign of Vijaya-Bukkarāya (Śaka 1331 to 1344). Registers the advent of a number of gauṇḍas from Nagara-śīma with their carts (i.e., baggage ?). to settle in the country ruled by Sōmaśaṅkara-Nāyaka of Ratnagiri. Three new villages were founded and village officers appoint-ed. Also mentions Malikībharāma-varāha (i.e., pagoda issued by the Golcoṇḍa king Malik Ibrāhīm).

B.--Stone inscriptions copied in 1912 (continued from last Annual Report).


ARIE/1912-1913/B/1912/98 (page 16)
Placement
On the south wall of the central shrine in the Ādhipurīśvara temple at Tiruvor-riyur.
Dynasty
Chōḷa
King
Tribhuvanachakravartin Rājādhirājadēva (II).
Date
3rd year
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Gift of 90 sheep for a lamp to the temple of Tiruv-oṟṟiyūr-Uḍeiyār at Tiruvoṟṟiyūr, a village in Puḻaṟ-kōṭṭam, which was a sub-division of Jayaṅgoṇḍaśōḻa maṇḍalam, by Vaḷḷaikiḻāṉ Mādavaṉ Paḍampakka-Nāyakaṉ alias Tiruchchiṟṟambala-Mūvēndavēḷāṉ, a native of Kaḍaṟpākkam.
ARIE/1912-1913/B/1912/99 (page 16)
Placement
On the same wall
Dynasty
Do.
King
Tribhuvanachakravartin Rājarājadēva (III)
Date
27th year, Dha-nus, ba. di. 2, Wednesday, Puṇarpūśam (= Wed. 10 Decr. 1242).
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Gift of 32 cows, a bull and a lamp-stand by a native of Ānāṉgūr in Paṉaiyūr-nāḍu, a sub-division of Naḍuvu-nāḍu alias Rājarāja-vaḷanāḍu. The donor was evidently residing at Koṉṟūr Villipākkam which was a sub-division of Ambattūr-nāḍu in the district of Puḻal-kōṭṭam alias Vikkiramaśōḻa-vaḷanāḍu in Jayaṅgoṇḍaśōḻa-maṇḍalam.

Tamil

Registers a sale of land by certain members of the assembly of Maṇali alias Śiṅgavishṇu-chaturvēdi-maṅgalam a dēvadāna village of the temple of Tiruvoṟṟiyūr-Uḍaiyār situated in Puḻal-nāḍu a sub-division of Puḻal-kōṭṭam which was a district of Jayaṅgoṇḍaśōḻa-maṇḍalam, to the military officer (taṇḍanāyagam) Parāntakamārāyaṉ alias Rājādhi-rāja-Nilagaṅgaraiyar, a resident of Śattimaṅgalam in Iṉṉambar-nāḍu which was a sub-division of Rājēndraśiṅga-vaḷanāḍu, a district of Śōḻa-maṇḍa-lam.

ARIE/1912-1913/B/1912/114 (page 18)
Placement
On the same wall
Dynasty
Chōḷa
King
Tribhuvanachakravartin Kulōttuṅga-Chōḷa-dēva (III).
Date
11th year
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Gift of 12 buffaloes (for a lamp) and a lamp-stand (shaped like himself) to Tiruvoṟṟiyūr-Uḍaiyār, by Tiruvaraṅgam-Uḍaiyāṉ alias Daṉmaparipālaṉ Rājādhirāja Malaiyarāyaṉ, son of Muṉaiyada-raiyaṉ alias Kulōttuṅgaśōḻa-Malaiyarāyaṉ of Naḍuvilmalai Tiruneḍumpiṟai in Perumūr-nāḍu, a sub-division of Maṇavil-kōṭṭam. Records also the gift of 12 buffaloes (for a lamp), a similar lamp-stand and a silver bugle (kāḷam) to the goddess Āḷuḍaiya-Nāchchiyār. The lamp-stands were called Daṉma-paripālaṉ after the donor.

31st year
Language

Remarks
Registers a sale of land by the assembly of the brah-madēya villages of Sundaraśōḻa-chaturvēdimaṅga-lam and Vāṉavaṉmahādēvi-chaturvēdimaṅgalam. It was purchased by Nāgalavvaichchāṉi alias Āriyammai wife of Prabhākara-Bhaṭṭa a resident of Mēgalāpuram in the Ārya-dēśa and a devotee of the temple of Tiruvoṟṟiyūruḍaiya-Mahādēva. The purchased land was given to the maṭha called Rājēndraśōḻaṉ which was built by that lady. Records also other sales of land to the same lady and for the same purpose, by the residents of Eṇṇūr in Nāvalūr-nāḍu which was a sub-division of Puḻār-kōṭṭam and by the merchants (nagarattār) of Tiru-voṟṟiyūr in the years 31 and 27 of the same reign, respectively.

Tribhuvanachakravartin Kōnērinmaikoṇḍāṉ (Kulōttuṅga III).
Date
38th year and 239th day.
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Gift of Kuḷattūr alias Kulōttuṅgaśōḻaṉ Kāvaṉūr (detached from Puṉṉaivāyil alias Rājanārāyaṇa-chaturvēdimaṅgalam) by Durgaiyāṇḍi-Nāyakaṉ, agent of Śittaraiśaṉ for the maintenance of the Vyākaraṇadāna-vyākhyāna-maṇḍapa built by him-self in the temple of Tiruvoṟṟiyūr. The officer Vāṇādarāyar and the tirumandira-ōlai, Neṟiyuḍai-chchōḻa-Mūvēndavēḷāṉ, are also mentioned.

King
Sakalalōkachakravartin Rājanārāyaṇaṉ Śambuvarāyar.
Date
12th year, Puraṭ-ṭādi, 1st day.
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Gift of land at Kaḍuvaṉkōṭṭam with the order of Tikkama-Nāyaka declaring the land tax-free, for offerings and festivals, by Vāgiśuradēva-Mudaliyār of Kīḻai-maḍam, while he was on his death-bed. The purchase of this land is stated to have been engraved on the stone wall of the Tirumūlattā-ṉamuḍaiya-Nāyaṉār temple at Puḻal. A portion of the land was also assigned to Aḻagiya-Tiruch-chiṟṟambalamuḍaiyār who was to succeed Vāgīśa as the head of that maṭha.

Tamil
Remarks

Tamil
Remarks
Gift of money for a lamp to the temple of Tirunīr-malai-Emberumāṉ, [at Tirunīrmalai] in Śurattūr-nāḍu of Puliyūr-kōṭṭam, a sub-division of Jayaṅ-goṇḍaśōḻa maṇḍalam, by Kaikaiyarāyaṉ Tiruva-gattīśuramuḍaiyāṉ of Malayambākkam in Māṅgā-ḍunāḍu of the same division.

Language
Sanskṛit & Kanarese
Remarks
Damaged. Records a gift to the shrines of Pāpavi-nāśadēva. Raghunāthadēva and Vīrēśvaradēva, by the mahājanas of Nagaragere alias Kṛishṇarāya samudra-agrahāra, a village in Roda-nāḍu which was a sub-division of Penugoṇḍe-rājya. The gift consisted of a talaparigi-channel below the tank of Nagaragere and of a tank called Gūḷiseṭikuṇṭe in Āḍabāṟahaḷḷi village. Mentions Vīrabhūpa the brother of Penugoṇḍe Vīrappaṇṇa who was the son of Nandi-Lakiseṭi of Lēpākshi.

Language
Sanskṛit & Kanarese
Remarks
Gift of tolls collected by the merchants at the market held every Sunday in the hamlet of Vīrēśvara-dēvarapura belonging to Lēpākshi, of tolls raised in Haru-nāḍu and Hosūra-nāḍu and of other income, for oblations to be offered in the three shrines mentioned above. The grant was made at the instance of Vīraṇa-Nāyaka, brother of Vīra-paṇṇaya of Penugoṇḍe.

Language
Sanskṛit & Kanarese
Remarks
Records a sale of land to the same three shrines by the mahājanas of the Sarvamānya-agrahāra village Kañchasamudra alias Pratāpadēvarāyapura which was given to them as a free gift by Pratāpa-dēva-Mahārāya when he made the great gifts named kāmadhēnu, kalpavṛiksha and viśvachakra in the presence of the god Virūpāksha on the banks of the Tuṅgabhadrā river. Lēpāksha is stated to have been a village in Sādali-vēṇṭe which belonged to Roda-nāḍu a sub-division of Penugoṇḍe-rājya.

Remarks
Gift by purchase from Bhaṇḍāra Timmapa, of the village Nandicherla alias Virūpākshapura, [near] Kārakalike in Buruḍakuṇṭe-rājya, to the god Vīrēśa who had bestowed favours on Vīrapaṇṇa, by the chief Achyutarāya Mallapaṇṇa devotee of Mallikārjuna. On the north wall of the central shrine in the Tiruvēlīśvara temple at Nanjai Edaiyar.
Dynasty
Chōḷa
King
Parakēsarivarman alias Rājēndra-Chōḷadēva (I).
Date
7th year
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Damaged and fragmentary. Seems to record a grant of land to the temple of Śrī-Kailāsam alias Tiruveyilvāyiluḍaiya-Paramēśvara, by the assembly of Rājēndrasiṁha-chaturvēdimaṅgalam. Men-tions Iḍaiyāṟu in Rājāśraya-vaḷanāḍu.
ARIE/1912-1913/C/1913/43 (page 74)
Placement
On a stone lying to the south of the Kuṇṇīśvara temple at Kunnamalai.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Vīrarājēndradēva (i.e., Kulōttuṅga-Chōḷa III).
Date
24th year
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Registers the name of a gāmiṇḍa (i.e. gauṇḍaṉ) who was one of the Veḷḷāḷas of Valipuram in Maḻai-nāḍu. Perhaps the stone was presented by him.

Placement
On the second gōpura of the same temple, left and right of entrance.

Chōḷa
King
Tribhuvanachakravartin Rājēndra-Chōḷa-dēva (III).
Date
4th year, Dha-nus, su. di. 3, Thursday, Tiruvōṇam.
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Damaged. Seems to record an enquiry into the affairs of the temple of Tirumāṇikkamalai-uḍaiya-Nāyaṉār in Kuṟukkai-nāḍu, a sub-division of Rājagaṁbhīra-vaḷanāḍu The committee of enquiry included the great minister Aḷiya-Sōmaya-Daṇḍanāyaka, Śēvaya-Daṇḍanāyaka and Sōmanā-tha-Viṭṭaya who was a servant in the palace of Sōmīśvaradēva.

Language
Tamil
Remarks
Gift of land to the temple of Gaṇa[pa]tīśuram-uḍaiya-Mahādēva at Tiruchcheṅgāṭṭaṅguḍi by the assembly of the village Tirukkaṇṇapuram a brahmadēya in Marugal-nāḍu which was a sub-division of Kshatriyaśikhāmaṇi vaḷanāḍu. ARIE/1912-1913/C/1913/65 (page 77)
Placement
On the same wall
Dynasty
Chōḷa
King
Parakēsarivaraman alias Tribhuvanachakra-vartin Kulōttuṅga-Chōḷadēva (III), ‘who took Madurai (Madura) and was pleased to take the crowned head of the Pāṇḍya.’
Date
[1]1th year and 175th day, Vṛiśchika, ba. di. 14, Fri-day, Aṉiḻam.
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Registers that a document connected with the temple of Tiruvirāmanandiśvaram-Uḍaiyār at Tirukkaṇ-ṇapuram a brahmadēya village of Marugal-nāḍu in Gēyamāṇikka-vaḷanāḍu, was engraved on the walls of the temple at Tiruchcheṅgāṭṭaṅguḍi, as the former was evidently not constructed of stone. The record refers to the 5th and 10th years of Periyadēvar Kulōttuṅga-Chōḷadēva in whose time the Tirukkaṇṇapuram temple came into existence.

ARIE/1912-1913/C/1913/93 (page 79)
Placement
On the third pillar lying in the same place.
Dynasty
Noḻamba (Pal-lava).
King
Iṟiva-Noḻambādhirāja
Date
Śaka 8[8]7, Krōdhana, Phālguṇa, Amāvāsyā, Sunday, solar eclipse.
Language
Kanarese
Remarks
Registers a gift of land for maintaining a tank, by prince Poḻalchōra, a grandson of the king and ‘the lord of Kāñchī’. The pillar was set up by Chā-vuṇḍayya of the Śrīvatsa-gōtra, the favourite minister of Poḻalchōra.

Language
Kanarese
Remarks
Gift of 50 varāhas (till now appropriated by the over-seers of temple affairs) to the temple of Mallikār-junadēva at Kambhadūru, by Vīrupaṇa-Nāyaka, for the merit of his father Tammapa-Nāyaka.

Dynasty
Vijayanagara
King
Vīrapratāpa Kṛishṇarāya-Mahārāya
Date
Śaka 1434, Āṅgīrasa, Kā-rttika, su. di. 12.
Language
Kanarese
Remarks
Gift of land by Rāyasta Koṇḍamarasay[y]a to the temple of Mallikārjunadēva at Kambhadūru, for the merit of the king. The land was situated below the tank of Kambhadūru in Kundurupiya-śīme which was the jāghir of the chief.
